    <article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-csci-1300-cs1-starting-computing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#csci-1300-cs1-starting-computing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>CSCI 1300 CS1: Starting Computing</strong></h4>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-naiduyehhoefer---fall-2022" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#naiduyehhoefer---fall-2022"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Naidu/Yeh/Hoefer - Fall 2022</strong></h4>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-homework-9" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#homework-9"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Homework 9</strong></h4>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-due-wednesday-december-7th-by-1159-pm" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#due-wednesday-december-7th-by-1159-pm"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Due: Wednesday, December 7th, by 11:59 pm</strong></h4>

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-table-of-contents" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#table-of-contents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Table of contents</h1>

<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-homework-summary-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#homework-summary-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Homework Summary <a name="user-content-summary"></a></h1>
<p dir="auto">For this assignment, we will be creating an aquarium planner to assist aquarists (people who own aquariums) in managing their fish. Question 0 will give you a brief overview of the class you will be creating, and the remaining questions will walk you through implementing each method of the <strong>Aquarium</strong> class.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> This assignment is a <strong>grade replacement</strong> and is not mandatory. If you complete this assignment, you can earn up to 45 points worth of extra credit. Note that you may not earn more than 325 total points for the homeworks. For example, if you currently have 300 points on the homeworks and earn all 45 points from this assignment, your score will max out at 325 total points.</p>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-objectives-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#objectives-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Objectives <a name="user-content-objectives"></a></h1>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Learn how to work with structs, objects, vectors, and file I/O.</li>
<li>Get some extra credit!</li>
</ol>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-background-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#background-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Background <a name="user-content-background"></a></h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-structures" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#structures"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Structures</strong></h2>
<p dir="auto">In C++, we can define a <strong>structure</strong> using the keyword <code>struct</code> like so:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="struct State
{
    string name;
    int area;
};                   // &lt;-- semicolon after struct definition"><pre><span class="pl-k">struct</span> <span class="pl-en">State</span>
{
    string name;
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> area;
};                   <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> &lt;-- semicolon after struct definition</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This defines a new type, <code>State</code>, that you can use for declaring variables, e.g.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//create a State variable with no name or area
State empty_state;

//create a State variable with a name and area
State colorado{&quot;Colorado&quot;, 104094};"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create a State variable with no name or area</span>
State empty_state;

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create a State variable with a name and area</span>
State colorado{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Colorado<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">104094</span>};</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The variables <code>empty_state</code> and <code>colorado</code> both have two named attributes, called <strong>members</strong> - <code>name</code> and <code>area</code>. We can access each member using dot notation, e.g.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//set members for empty State
empty_state.name = &quot;Texas&quot;;
empty_state.area = 268596;

//get members for colorado
cout &lt;&lt; colorado.name &lt;&lt; &quot; has an area of&quot; &lt;&lt; colorado.area &lt;&lt; &quot; square miles.&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>set members for empty State</span>
empty_state.name = <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Texas<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
empty_state.area = <span class="pl-c1">268596</span>;

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>get members for colorado</span>
cout &lt;&lt; colorado.name &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span> has an area of<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; colorado.area &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span> square miles.<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Expected output:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Colorado has an area of 104094 square miles."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Colorado has an area of 104094 square miles.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">If we want to compare two structs, we cannot do so directly. Instead, we must compare each data member individually to see if they match, e.g.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//check each data member by one
if(colorado.name == emptyState.name &amp;&amp; colorado.area == emptyState.area)
{
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;These are the same state!&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;
}
else
{
    cout &lt;&lt; &quot;These are not the same state!&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>check each data member by one</span>
<span class="pl-k">if</span>(colorado.name == emptyState.name &amp;&amp; colorado.area == emptyState.area)
{
    cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>These are the same state!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;
}
<span class="pl-k">else</span>
{
    cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>These are not the same state!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Expected output:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="These are not the same state!"><pre class="notranslate"><code>These are not the same state!
</code></pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-structs-and-classes" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#structs-and-classes"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Structs and Classes</strong></h2>
<p dir="auto">A class can have a <code>struct</code> as a data member, much like how a class could have any other type of data member. It's important to make sure that the class header file (the .h file) can see the definition of the struct. This can be accomplished by defining the struct inside of the .h file, like below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// filename: example.h
struct State
{
    string name;
    int area;
};                // don't forget the semicolon

class Example
{
    private:
        State my_state_;
        //other data members

    public:
        //setter accepts a State parameter
        void setState(State new_state);

        //getter returns the State member variable
        State getState();

        //other member methods
};"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> filename: example.h</span>
<span class="pl-k">struct</span> <span class="pl-en">State</span>
{
    string name;
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> area;
};                <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> don't forget the semicolon</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Example</span>
{
    <span class="pl-k">private:</span>
        State my_state_;
        <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>other data members</span>

    <span class="pl-k">public:</span>
        <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>setter accepts a State parameter</span>
        <span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">setState</span>(State new_state);

        <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>getter returns the State member variable</span>
        State <span class="pl-en">getState</span>();

        <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>other member methods</span>
};</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Any file that includes the .h file shown above will be able to use instances of the <code>State</code> struct, so you will not need to define the <code>State</code> struct anywhere else.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-vectors-of-structs" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#vectors-of-structs"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Vectors of Structs</strong></h2>
<p dir="auto">Much like how we can have vectors of objects, we can also have vectors of structs. We would define a vector of structs like so:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="struct State
{
    string name;
    int area;
};

//create a vector of States
vector&lt;State&gt; my_states;

//add a state to the vector
State new_state{&quot;Random State&quot;, 123};
my_states.push_back(new_state);"><pre><span class="pl-k">struct</span> <span class="pl-en">State</span>
{
    string name;
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> area;
};

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create a vector of States</span>
vector&lt;State&gt; my_states;

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>add a state to the vector</span>
State new_state{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Random State<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">123</span>};
my_states.push_back(new_state);</pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-when-to-use-structs-versus-classes" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#when-to-use-structs-versus-classes"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>When to Use Structs Versus Classes</strong></h2>
<p dir="auto">While structs and classes are similar, there are some key differences between them. When deciding whether you should use one over the other, consider the functionality you'd like to achieve. A good rule of thumb is to ask whether the data type you're defining will need to have any methods or private variables. If it will, then you should create a class. If all members can be public and there are no methods, then a struct may be better.</p>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-testing-functions-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#testing-functions-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Testing functions <a name="user-content-tests"></a></h1>
<p dir="auto">Every C++ program you write should include a main function that tests the function you wrote.
There will be different types of test cases you will write depending on the return type of the function.
Listed below is how we expect you to test different types of functions. The process will be different for testing a <code>void</code> function, functions that return an <code>int</code> or <code>bool</code>, and functions
that return a <code>double</code>.</p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-1-void-functions-with-printed-output-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#1-void-functions-with-printed-output-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>1. Void Functions with printed output <a name="user-content-void"></a></h4>
<p dir="auto">For <strong>void</strong> functions that have printed output (i.e. functions that use <code>cout</code> to print to the terminal), call the testing function in the main function. Your tests should include the expected output in comments.</p>
<p dir="auto">See the sample code below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="void checkDiscount(double discount) {
    if (discount &gt;= 50) {
        cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Great discount!&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;
    } else {
        cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Not a great discount.&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;
    }
    return;
}
int main() {
    // test 1 for checkDiscount
    // expected output: &quot;Great discount!&quot;
    checkDiscount(82.7);
    
    // test 2 for checkDiscount
    // expected output: &quot;Not a great discount.&quot;
    checkDiscount(22);
    
    return 0;
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">checkDiscount</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> discount) {
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> (discount &gt;= <span class="pl-c1">50</span>) {
        cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Great discount!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;
    } <span class="pl-k">else</span> {
        cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Not a great discount.<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;
    }
    <span class="pl-k">return</span>;
}
<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>() {
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 1 for checkDiscount</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> expected output: "Great discount!"</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">checkDiscount</span>(<span class="pl-c1">82.7</span>);
    
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 2 for checkDiscount</span>
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> expected output: "Not a great discount."</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">checkDiscount</span>(<span class="pl-c1">22</span>);
    
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>* For the purpose of this test code snippet, algorithm comments were not included, but they are still expected in your C++ files.</em></p>
<br>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-2-non-void-functions-returning-bool-or-int-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#2-non-void-functions-returning-bool-or-int-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>2. Non-Void Functions returning bool or int <a name="user-content-non-void-bool-int"></a></h4>
<p dir="auto">For functions that return a <strong>bool, char or int</strong>, use <strong>assert statements</strong>
from the <strong>cassert</strong> library (<code>#include &lt;cassert&gt;</code>) with a conditional expression.</p>
<p dir="auto">Assert statements contain a conditional expression which will evaluate to <code>true</code> if the function's actual output matches what's expected. If the conditional expression evaluates to <code>false</code>, then your program will stop running after printing an error message.</p>
<p dir="auto">For the purpose of this project, functions that return a <code>bool</code>, <code>char</code> or <code>int</code> can be compared to a specific value using the equality operator <code>==</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Your test will look something like this:</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>assert(&lt;function call&gt; == &lt;value to compare to&gt;);</code></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>&lt;function call&gt;</code> is where you will call the function you want to test with its function parameters.</li>
<li><code>&lt;value to compare to&gt;</code> is the value you expect the function to return.</li>
<li><code>==</code> is the equality operator, and it compares the equality of both sides of itself.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">See the sample code below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#include &lt;iostream&gt;
#include &lt;cassert&gt;
using namespace std;

int addInts(int num1, int num2)
{
    // add num1 and num2 before returning
    return num1 + num2;
}

// isDrivingAge() returns true if the given age passed as a parameter
// is greater than or equal to 16, otherwise it returns false.
bool isDrivingAge(int age)
{
    return age &gt;= 16;
}

int main()
{
    // test 1 for addInts
    assert(addInts(5, 6) == 11);

    // test 2 for addInts
    assert(addInts(10, 10) == 20);

    // test 3 for drivingAge
    assert(isDrivingAge(17) == true);

    // test 4 for drivingAge
    assert(isDrivingAge(14) == false);
}"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>iostream<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>cassert<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> <span class="pl-k">namespace</span> <span class="pl-en">std</span><span class="pl-k">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">addInts</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> num1, <span class="pl-k">int</span> num2)
{
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> add num1 and num2 before returning</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> num1 + num2;
}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> isDrivingAge() returns true if the given age passed as a parameter</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> is greater than or equal to 16, otherwise it returns false.</span>
<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-en">isDrivingAge</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> age)
{
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> age &gt;= <span class="pl-c1">16</span>;
}

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>()
{
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 1 for addInts</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">addInts</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>, <span class="pl-c1">6</span>) == <span class="pl-c1">11</span>);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 2 for addInts</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">addInts</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>, <span class="pl-c1">10</span>) == <span class="pl-c1">20</span>);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 3 for drivingAge</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">isDrivingAge</span>(<span class="pl-c1">17</span>) == <span class="pl-c1">true</span>);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 4 for drivingAge</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">isDrivingAge</span>(<span class="pl-c1">14</span>) == <span class="pl-c1">false</span>);
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>* For the purpose of this test code snippet, algorithm comments were not included, but they are still expected in your C++ files.</em></p>
<br>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-3-non-void-functions-returning-double-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#3-non-void-functions-returning-double-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>3. Non-Void Functions returning double <a name="user-content-non-void-double"></a></h4>
<p dir="auto">For functions that return a <strong>double</strong>, you should use an <strong>assert statement</strong> from the <strong>cassert</strong> header (<code>#include &lt;cassert&gt;</code>) with a conditional expression like above. The difference is that you will also need to include the following function in your program:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="/**
 * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.
 */
bool doublesEqual(double a, double b, const double epsilon = 1e-2)
{
    double c = a - b;
    return c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-en">doublesEqual</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> a, <span class="pl-k">double</span> b, <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-k">double</span> epsilon = <span class="pl-c1">1e-2</span>)
{
    <span class="pl-k">double</span> c = a - b;
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Because the <code>double</code> type holds so much precision, it will be hard to compare the equality of a function that returns a
double with another double value. To overcome this challenge, we can compare <code>double</code> values within a certain range
of precision or decimal places. The function above compares the equality of two variables <code>a</code> and <code>b</code> up to two decimal places, and returns <code>true</code> if the values of <code>a</code> and <code>b</code> are equal with each other up to two decimal places.</p>
<p dir="auto">You will be expected to use this function in conjunction with <code>assert</code> statements to test functions that return
the type double.</p>
<p dir="auto">Your test will look something like this:</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>assert(doubles_equal(&lt;function call&gt;, &lt;value to compare to&gt;));</code></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>&lt;function call&gt;</code> is where you will call the function you want to test with its function parameters</li>
<li><code>&lt;value to compare to&gt;</code> is the <code>double</code> value you expect the function to return.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">See the sample code below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#include &lt;iostream&gt;
#include &lt;cassert&gt;
using namespace std;
/**
 * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.
 */
bool doublesEqual(double a, double b, const double epsilon = 1e-2)
{
    double c = a - b;
    return c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}
/**
 * reciprocal returns the value of 1 divided by the number passed into the function.
 */
double reciprocal(int num)
{
    return 1.0 / num;
}
int main()
{
    // test 1 for reciprocal
    assert(doublesEqual(reciprocal(6), 0.16));
    // test 2 for reciprocal
    assert(doublesEqual(reciprocal(12), 0.083));
}"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>iostream<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>cassert<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> <span class="pl-k">namespace</span> <span class="pl-en">std</span><span class="pl-k">;</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-en">doublesEqual</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> a, <span class="pl-k">double</span> b, <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-k">double</span> epsilon = <span class="pl-c1">1e-2</span>)
{
    <span class="pl-k">double</span> c = a - b;
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * reciprocal returns the value of 1 divided by the number passed into the function.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">double</span> <span class="pl-en">reciprocal</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> num)
{
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-c1">1.0</span> / num;
}
<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>()
{
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 1 for reciprocal</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(<span class="pl-c1">reciprocal</span>(<span class="pl-c1">6</span>), <span class="pl-c1">0.16</span>));
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 2 for reciprocal</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(<span class="pl-c1">reciprocal</span>(<span class="pl-c1">12</span>), <span class="pl-c1">0.083</span>));
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">For test 1, <code>reciprocal(6)</code> is being called, and we expect the function to return the value <code>0.16</code>.
The return value of <code>reciprocal(6)</code> and <code>0.16</code> is passed in as parameters to the <code>doublesEquals</code> function,
which will then return <code>true</code> if these two values are equal or <code>false</code> if they are not.</p>
<p dir="auto"><em>* For the purpose of this test code snippet, algorithm comments were not included, but they are still expected in your C++ files.</em>
<br></p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-4-functions-manipulating-arrays-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#4-functions-manipulating-arrays-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>4. Functions manipulating arrays <a name="user-content-test-function-array"></a></h4>
<p dir="auto">Functions which manipulate arrays passed as arguments can be tested by asserting on individual elements of the array after calling the function. This works even for <code>void</code> functions because arrays are passed by reference; even if the function doesn't return anything, the array in the function is the same array in memory as the one outside the scope of your function.</p>
<p dir="auto">Note that if the array is an array of <code>float</code> or <code>double</code>, the <code>doubles_equal</code> function described <a href="#non-void-double">here</a> should be used to assert on individual array elements.</p>
<p dir="auto">See the sample code below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#include&lt;iostream&gt;
#include&lt;cassert&gt;
using namespace std;

/**
 * Add one to each element of the array.
 */
void addOneToArrayElements(int arr[], int size) 
{
    for (int i = 0; i &lt; size; i++) 
    {
        arr[i] = arr[i] + 1;
    }
}

/**
 * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.
 */
bool doublesEqual(double a, double b, const double epsilon = 1e-2)
{
    double c = a - b;
    return c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}

/**
 * Add one to each element of the array.
 */
void addOneToArrayElementsDouble(double arr[], int size)
{
    for (int i = 0; i &lt; size; i++) 
    {
        arr[i] = arr[i] + 1.0;
    }
}

int main() 
{
    // test 1 for addOneToArrayElements
    int test1Arr[3] = {1, 2, 3};
    addOneToArrayElements(test1Arr, 3);
    assert(test1Arr[0] == 2);
    assert(test1Arr[1] == 3);
    assert(test1Arr[2] == 4);

    // test 2 for addOneToArrayElements
    int test2Arr[3] = {8, 10};
    addOneToArrayElements(test2Arr, 2);
    assert(test2Arr[0] == 9);
    assert(test2Arr[1] == 11);

    // test 1 for addOneToArrayElementsDouble
    double test3Arr[4] = {1.5, 4.6, 9.7, 16.8};
    addOneToArrayElementsDouble(testArr3, 4);
    assert(doublesEqual(testArr3[0], 2.5));
    assert(doublesEqual(testArr3[1], 5.6));
    assert(doublesEqual(testArr3[2], 10.7));
    assert(doublesEqual(testArr3[3], 17.8));
}"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">include</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>iostream<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
#<span class="pl-k">include</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>cassert<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">using</span> <span class="pl-k">namespace</span> <span class="pl-en">std</span><span class="pl-k">;</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * Add one to each element of the array.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">addOneToArrayElements</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> arr[], <span class="pl-k">int</span> size) 
{
    <span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">int</span> i = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>; i &lt; size; i++) 
    {
        arr[i] = arr[i] + <span class="pl-c1">1</span>;
    }
}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * doublesEqual will test if two doubles are equal to each other within two decimal places.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-en">doublesEqual</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> a, <span class="pl-k">double</span> b, <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-k">double</span> epsilon = <span class="pl-c1">1e-2</span>)
{
    <span class="pl-k">double</span> c = a - b;
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> c &lt; epsilon &amp;&amp; -c &lt; epsilon;
}

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span>*</span>
<span class="pl-c"> * Add one to each element of the array.</span>
<span class="pl-c"> <span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">addOneToArrayElementsDouble</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> arr[], <span class="pl-k">int</span> size)
{
    <span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">int</span> i = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>; i &lt; size; i++) 
    {
        arr[i] = arr[i] + <span class="pl-c1">1.0</span>;
    }
}

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>() 
{
    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 1 for addOneToArrayElements</span>
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> test1Arr[<span class="pl-c1">3</span>] = {<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-c1">3</span>};
    <span class="pl-c1">addOneToArrayElements</span>(test1Arr, <span class="pl-c1">3</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(test1Arr[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>] == <span class="pl-c1">2</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(test1Arr[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] == <span class="pl-c1">3</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(test1Arr[<span class="pl-c1">2</span>] == <span class="pl-c1">4</span>);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 2 for addOneToArrayElements</span>
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> test2Arr[<span class="pl-c1">3</span>] = {<span class="pl-c1">8</span>, <span class="pl-c1">10</span>};
    <span class="pl-c1">addOneToArrayElements</span>(test2Arr, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(test2Arr[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>] == <span class="pl-c1">9</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(test2Arr[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] == <span class="pl-c1">11</span>);

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> test 1 for addOneToArrayElementsDouble</span>
    <span class="pl-k">double</span> test3Arr[<span class="pl-c1">4</span>] = {<span class="pl-c1">1.5</span>, <span class="pl-c1">4.6</span>, <span class="pl-c1">9.7</span>, <span class="pl-c1">16.8</span>};
    <span class="pl-c1">addOneToArrayElementsDouble</span>(testArr3, <span class="pl-c1">4</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(testArr3[<span class="pl-c1">0</span>], <span class="pl-c1">2.5</span>));
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(testArr3[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>], <span class="pl-c1">5.6</span>));
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(testArr3[<span class="pl-c1">2</span>], <span class="pl-c1">10.7</span>));
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(<span class="pl-c1">doublesEqual</span>(testArr3[<span class="pl-c1">3</span>], <span class="pl-c1">17.8</span>));
}</pre></div>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-5-testing-class-objects-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#5-testing-class-objects-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>5. Testing class objects <a name="user-content-test-objects"></a></h4>
<p dir="auto">When creating an instance of a class, or an object, the attributes of that object can be tested
by asserting on the individual attributes or data members.</p>
<p dir="auto">Note that if the data attribute is a float or double, the doubles_equal function described <a href="#non-void-double">here</a>
should be used to assert on the value.</p>
<p dir="auto">Additionally, note that if the data attribute is an array, follow the <a href="#test-function-array">"Functions manipulating arrays" section</a>
on how to assert on individual array elements.</p>
<p dir="auto">See the sample code below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Animal
{
private:
    string sound_;
    string name_;
    int age_;

public:
    Animal();
    Animal(string, string, int);

    string getSound();
    string getName();
    int getAge();
};

Animal::Animal()
{
    sound_ = &quot;&quot;;
    name_ = &quot;&quot;;
    age_ = 0;
}

Animal::Animal(string sound, string name, int age)
{
    sound_ = sound;
    name_ = name;
    age_ = age;
}

string Animal::getSound()
{
    return sound_;
}

string Animal::getName()
{
    return name_;
}

int Animal::getAge()
{
    return age_;
}

int main()
{
    Animal default_dog;
    assert(default_dog.getSound() == &quot;&quot;);
    assert(default_dog.getAge() == 0);
    assert(default_dog.getName() == &quot;&quot;);

    Animal actual_dog(&quot;Bark bark!&quot;, &quot;Pluto&quot;, 2);
    assert(actual_dog.getSound() == &quot;Bark bark!&quot;);
    assert(actual_dog.getAge() == 2);
    assert(actual_dog.getName() == &quot;Pluto&quot;);
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Animal</span>
{
<span class="pl-k">private:</span>
    string sound_;
    string name_;
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> age_;

<span class="pl-k">public:</span>
    <span class="pl-en">Animal</span>();
    <span class="pl-en">Animal</span>(string, string, <span class="pl-k">int</span>);

    string <span class="pl-en">getSound</span>();
    string <span class="pl-en">getName</span>();
    <span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">getAge</span>();
};

<span class="pl-en">Animal::Animal</span>()
{
    sound_ = <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
    name_ = <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
    age_ = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;
}

<span class="pl-en">Animal::Animal</span>(string sound, string name, <span class="pl-k">int</span> age)
{
    sound_ = sound;
    name_ = name;
    age_ = age;
}

string <span class="pl-en">Animal::getSound</span>()
{
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> sound_;
}

string <span class="pl-en">Animal::getName</span>()
{
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> name_;
}

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">Animal::getAge</span>()
{
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> age_;
}

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>()
{
    Animal default_dog;
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(default_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getSound</span>() == <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(default_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getAge</span>() == <span class="pl-c1">0</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(default_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getName</span>() == <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

    Animal <span class="pl-smi">actual_dog</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Bark bark!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Pluto<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(actual_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getSound</span>() == <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Bark bark!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(actual_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getAge</span>() == <span class="pl-c1">2</span>);
    <span class="pl-c1">assert</span>(actual_dog.<span class="pl-c1">getName</span>() == <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Pluto<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><em>* For the purpose of this test code snippet, algorithm comments were not included, but they are still expected in your C++ files.</em></p>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-questions-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#questions-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Questions <a name="user-content-questions"></a></h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-0-0-points-the-fish-struct-and-aquarium-class-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-0-0-points-the-fish-struct-and-aquarium-class-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 0 (0 points): The <code>Fish</code> Struct and <code>Aquarium</code> Class</strong> <a name="user-content-q0"></a></h2>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-1-3-points-the-aquarium-constructor-getaquaristname-and-getgallonsused-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-1-3-points-the-aquarium-constructor-getaquaristname-and-getgallonsused-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 1 (3 points): The <code>Aquarium</code> Constructor, <code>getAquaristName</code> and <code>getGallonsUsed</code></strong> <a name="user-content-q1"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question, you will create three methods for the <code>Aquarium</code> class. The function specifications are listed below:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The <code>Aquarium</code> constructor</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">This constructor will accept one <code>string</code> parameter for the aquarist's name, and set <code>gallons_used</code> to 0.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept one parameter:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>string</code>: The name of the aquarist. The data member <code>aquarist_name</code> should be set to this parameter.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Set the <code>gallons_used</code> data member to 0.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The <code>getAquaristName</code> method</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">This method should accept no parameters and returns the <code>aquarist_name</code> data member.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept no parameters.</li>
<li>This function returns the <code>aquarist_name</code> data member as a <code>string</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The <code>getGallonsUsed</code> method</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">This method accepts no parameters and returns the <code>gallons_used</code> data member.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept no parameters.</li>
<li>This function returns the <code>gallons_used</code> data member as an <code>int</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example Usage</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//create an aquarium object

//test getGallonsUsed method
cout &lt;&lt; billys_aquarium.getGallonsUsed() &lt;&lt; endl;"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create an aquarium object</span>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-2-6-points-the-loadfish-method-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-2-6-points-the-loadfish-method-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 2 (6 points): The <code>loadFish</code> Method</strong> <a name="user-content-q2"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question you will implement the <code>loadFish</code> member method. This method should:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept one parameter:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>string</code>: The filepath to be read from</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Use <code>ifstream</code> and <code>getline</code> to read data from the file, creating a new <code>Fish</code> struct for each line, and put that struct into the <code>available_fish</code> member vector.</li>
<li>Empty lines should not be added to the vector.</li>
<li>You may assume that each non-empty line will contain valid data, i.e. each non-empty line will consist of a Fish name, and the gallons of water required for that Fish, separated by a comma. There will be exactly one comma on each line.</li>
<li>Fish names may have spaces in them, e.g. "Elephant Ear Guppy" is one of the fish names.</li>
<li>Assume that the txt files provided do <strong>not</strong> have duplicate fish listed.</li>
<li>You should use the <code>stoi()</code> method to convert the number of gallons of water required for each Fish from a <code>string</code> to an <code>int</code>.</li>
<li><strong>Hint</strong>: You can use the <code>split()</code> function from Homework 5 with a comma (<code>,</code>) as the delimiter.</li>
<li>This function should return:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>true</code> if the file was opened successfully</li>
<li><code>false</code> otherwise</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">We have provided an example <a href="/CSCI1300-StartingComputing/CSCI1300-Fall2022/blob/main/homework/homework9/data_files/fish_example.txt">fish_example.txt</a> file for you to use while developing your solution. A preview of this file is displayed below:</p>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-3-3-points-the-displayavailablefish-method-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-3-3-points-the-displayavailablefish-method-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 3 (3 points): The <code>displayAvailableFish</code> Method</strong> <a name="user-content-q3"></a></h2>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-4-6-points-the-addfish-method-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-4-6-points-the-addfish-method-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 4 (6 points): The <code>addFish</code> Method</strong> <a name="user-content-q4"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question you will implement the <code>addFish</code> member method. This method should:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept one parameter:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>string</code>: The name of the Fish to be added to the aquarium.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The function should look through the <code>available_fish</code> vector to ensure that this Fish is available to add to the aquarium
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Note:</strong> The Fish name should be case <strong>insensitive</strong>, e.g. both "Elephant Ear Guppy" and "elePHant eaR guPPY" refer to the same Fish.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If the Fish is available to add, the method should add the Fish to the <code>selected_fish</code> data member.
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Be sure to update the <code>gallons_used</code> data member appropriately!</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If the Fish has been added to the Aquarium successfully, the Fish should be removed from the <code>available_fish</code> member vector.</li>
<li><strong>Note:</strong> The number of gallons used by the fish cannot exceed the maximum tank size, which is stored in the constant data member <code>tank_size_gallons</code>. If adding the Fish to the Aquarium would result in too many <code>gallons_used</code>, then this function should <strong>not</strong> add the Fish to the aquarium.</li>
<li>The function should return one of the following <code>int</code> values:
<ul dir="auto">
<li>-1 if the Fish is not available to add to the Aquarium</li>
<li>0 if the Fish is available but there isn't enough space the Aquarium (ie, <code>gallons_used</code> would be more than <code>tank_size_gallons</code>)</li>
<li>1 if the Fish was successfully added to the Aquarium.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example Usage</strong></p>

<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-5-6-points-the-removefish-method-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-5-6-points-the-removefish-method-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 5 (6 points): The <code>removeFish</code> Method</strong> <a name="user-content-q5"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question you will implement the <code>removeFish</code> method. This method should:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept one parameter:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>string</code>: The fish to be removed from the aquarium.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>This function should search through the <code>selected_fish</code> data member to find the appropriate fish to remove.
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Note:</strong> The fish name should be case <strong>insensitive</strong>, e.g. both "minnow" and "Minnow" refer to the same fish.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>If the fish is currently selected, it should be removed from the <code>selected_fish</code> data member.
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Be sure to update the <code>gallons_used</code> data member appropriately!</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Once the Fish has been removed, it should be put back into the <code>available_fish</code> data member, so that the fish may be re-selected if desired.</li>
<li>The function should return one of the following <code>bool</code> values:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>true</code> if the fish was removed successfully</li>
<li><code>false</code> otherwise. This includes the case where the fish does not exist at all.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example Usage</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//create an aquarium object
Aquarium marias_fish(&quot;maria&quot;);

//load fish
marias_fish.loadFish(&quot;fish_15.txt&quot;);

//add a fish
marias_fish.addFish(&quot;Cardinal Tetra&quot;);

//remove fish that has not been selected
cout &lt;&lt; marias_fish.removeFish(&quot;Butterfly Koi&quot;) &lt;&lt; endl;

// remove fish that has been selected
cout &lt;&lt; marias_fish.removeFish(&quot;Cardinal Tetra&quot;) &lt;&lt; endl;"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create an aquarium object</span>
Aquarium <span class="pl-en">marias_fish</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>maria<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>load fish</span>
marias_fish.loadFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fish_15.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>add a fish</span>
marias_fish.addFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Cardinal Tetra<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>remove fish that has not been selected</span>
cout &lt;&lt; marias_fish.removeFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Butterfly Koi<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) &lt;&lt; endl;

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> remove fish that has been selected</span>
cout &lt;&lt; marias_fish.removeFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Cardinal Tetra<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) &lt;&lt; endl;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Expected output:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="0
1"><pre class="notranslate"><code>0
1
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When you are done implementing this method, head on over to Coderunner and paste all of your .h file contents and the implementation for <strong>all of the member methods from questions 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5</strong> into the answer box. Do not paste in any <code>#include</code> directives or <code>using namespace std;</code> into the CodeRunner - that's already been included for you. There is nothing to submit to Canvas for this question; you will submit your <code>Aquarium.h</code> and <code>Aquarium.cpp</code> files to Canvas once you have finished implementing all of the member methods.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-6-5-points-the-writeaquariumcontents-method-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-6-5-points-the-writeaquariumcontents-method-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 6 (5 points): The <code>writeAquariumContents</code> Method</strong> <a name="user-content-q6"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question you will implement the <code>writeAquariumContents</code> member method. This method should:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Accept one parameter:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>string</code>: The filepath for the output to be saved.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>This function should write a list of the Fish currently in the Aquarium to the file specified by the filepath.</li>
<li>This method should output the following to the specified txt file:
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If there are no Fish in the Aquarium, the function should write <code>There are no fish in &lt;aquarist's name&gt;'s Aquarium.</code>.</li>
<li>Otherwise, the function should write <code>&lt;aquarist's name&gt;'s Aquarium (&lt;gallons_used&gt; of &lt;tank_size_gallons&gt; gallons of water used):</code> on the first line, followed by the Fish name and gallons required, one per line.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>This function should return one of the following <code>bool</code> values:
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>true</code> if the aquarium's contents were written to the file successfully (regardless of whether or not there are any fish in the aquarium).</li>
<li><code>false</code> if the file could not be opened.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example 1:</strong> Multiple Fish in the Aquarium.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//create an aquarium object
Aquarium billys_aquarium(&quot;Billy&quot;);

billys_aquarium.addFish(&quot;Blue Peacock Cichlid&quot;);

billys_aquarium.writeAquariumContents(&quot;billysAquarium.txt&quot;);"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create an aquarium object</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>load fish from file</span>
billys_aquarium.loadFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fish_example.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>add some fish</span>
billys_aquarium.addFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>platinum ogon koi<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
billys_aquarium.addFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>eLePhAnt EaR bEtTa<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
billys_aquarium.addFish(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Blue Peacock Cichlid<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

billys_aquarium.writeAquariumContents(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>billysAquarium.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Expected contents of <code>billysAquarium.txt</code>:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Billy's Aquarium (11 of 12 gallons of water used):
Platinum Ogon Koi - 5
Elephant Ear Betta - 3

Platinum Ogon Koi - 5
Elephant Ear Betta - 3
Blue Peacock Cichlid - 3
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example 2:</strong> The Aquarium is empty (no fish).</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="//create aquarium object
Aquarium billys_aquarium(&quot;Billy&quot;);

//save aquarium contents
billys_aquarium.writeAquariumContents(&quot;billysAquarium.txt&quot;);"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>create aquarium object</span>
Aquarium <span class="pl-en">billys_aquarium</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Billy<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span>save aquarium contents</span>
billys_aquarium.writeAquariumContents(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>billysAquarium.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Expected contents of <code>billysAquarium.txt</code>:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="There are no fish in Billy's Aquarium."><pre class="notranslate"><code>There are no fish in Billy's Aquarium.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When you are done implementing this method, head on over to Coderunner and paste <strong>the entirety</strong> of your header (Aquarium.h) and implementation (Aquarium.cpp) files into the answer box. Do not paste in any <code>#include</code> directives or <code>using namespace std;</code> into the CodeRunner - that's already been included for you. You will submit your (now completed) Aquarium.h and Aquarium.cpp files to Canvas for this question, along with a aquariumDriver.cpp file that tests out your new Aquarium class (See the <a href="#test-objects">testing class objects</a> section above for more details about how to test your new class).</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-question-7-6-points-an-aquarium-menu-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#question-7-6-points-an-aquarium-menu-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a><strong>Question 7 (6 points): An Aquarium Menu</strong> <a name="user-content-q7"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">For this question, you will create a file called <strong>aquariumMenu.cpp</strong> that will provide a menu for an aquarist to manage their aquarium. In this file, you should create a main function that begins by prompting the user for their name:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Welcome to the aquarium manager. Please enter the aquarist's name:"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Welcome to the aquarium manager. Please enter the aquarist's name:
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Once the user has entered their name, your program should create an <code>Aquarium</code> object with the attribute <code>aquarist_name</code> set to the name entered by the user. Then, your program should display the following menu:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="--Aquarium Manager--
1. Load fish
2. Display available fish
3. Add a fish
4. Remove a fish
5. Save aquarium contents
6. Exit"><pre class="notranslate"><code>--Aquarium Manager--
1. Load fish
2. Display available fish
3. Add a fish
4. Remove a fish
5. Save aquarium contents
6. Exit
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This menu should run on a loop, continually displaying the options above until the user chooses to exit. You should make use of the functions you wrote previously, call them with appropriate input, and process the values they return. The behavior of each menu optioon is explained below:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 1: loadFish</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Prompt the user for a file path:</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Please enter a filepath:"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Please enter a filepath:
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Pass the file path to your <code>loadFish</code> member function.</li>
<li>If <code>loadFish</code> returns <code>true</code>, print:</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Fish loaded successfully."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Fish loaded successfully.
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If <code>loadFish</code> returns <code>false</code>, print:</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Could not open file. No fish loaded."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Could not open file. No fish loaded.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 2: Display available fish</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Call your <code>displayAvailableFish</code> member function.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 3: Add a fish</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Prompt the user to enter the fish they want to add:</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Which fish would you like to add?"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Which fish would you like to add?
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Use your <code>addFish</code> member function to add the fish to the aquarium.</li>
<li>If <code>addFish</code> returns -1, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Could not find fish: &lt;fish name&gt;."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Could not find fish: &lt;fish name&gt;.
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If <code>addFish</code> returns 0, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="The aquarium is already at &lt;gallons_used&gt; gallons and this fish cannot be added."><pre class="notranslate"><code>The aquarium is already at &lt;gallons_used&gt; gallons and this fish cannot be added.
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If <code>addFish</code> returns 1, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Fish added successfully."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Fish added successfully.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 4: Remove Fish</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Prompt the user to enter the fish they would like to remove:</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Which fish would you like to remove?"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Which fish would you like to remove?
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Use your <code>removeFish</code> member function to remove the Fish from the aquarium.</li>
<li>If <code>removeFish</code> returns <code>false</code>, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="&lt;fish name&gt; not found."><pre class="notranslate"><code>&lt;fish name&gt; not found.
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If <code>removeFish</code> returns <code>true</code>, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Fish removed successfully."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Fish removed successfully.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 5: Save aquarium contents</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Prompt the user for a file path</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Where would you like to save your aquarium?"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Where would you like to save your aquarium?
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Pass the file path to your <code>writeAquariumContents</code> member function.</li>
<li>If <code>writeAquariumContents returns </code>false`, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Could not open file. Aquarium was not saved."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Could not open file. Aquarium was not saved.
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>If <code>writeAquariumContents</code> returns <code>true</code>, print</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Aquarium saved successfully."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Aquarium saved successfully.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Option 6: Exit</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Display a parting message</li>
</ul>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Goodbye!"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Goodbye!
</code></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>End the program.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Invalid input</strong>
If the user inputs a value that is not one of the menu options, print</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Invalid input. Please enter a number between 1 and 6."><pre class="notranslate"><code>Invalid input. Please enter a number between 1 and 6.
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And then display the menu again. Assume menu input will always be numeric.</p>
<p dir="auto">Below is a <strong>sample run</strong> of the <code>aquariumMenu.cpp</code> program. User input is in <strong>bold</strong>.</p>

3. Add a fish
4. Remove a fish
5. Save aquarium contents
6. Exit
<b>2</b>
Fish available to add to aquarium:
Minnow - 1
Fancy Guppy - 1
Blue Neon Guppy - 1
Elephant Ear Guppy - 2
Yellow Guppy - 1
Lyretail Guppy - 1

Electric Green Longfin Tetra - 2

--Aquarium Manager--

2. Display available fish

--Aquarium Manager--
1. Load fish
2. Display available fish
3. Add a fish
4. Remove a fish
5. Save aquarium contents
6. Exit
<b>6</b>
Goodbye!</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Expected contents of <code>aquariumSchedule.txt</code></strong>:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Emily Voigt's Aquarium  (8 of 12 gallons of water used):
Halfmoon Betta - 4
Blue Crowntail Betta - 4"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Emily Voigt's Aquarium  (8 of 12 gallons of water used):
Halfmoon Betta - 4
Blue Crowntail Betta - 4
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When you are done implementing this method, head on over to Coderunner and paste <strong>the entirety</strong> of your header (Aquarium.h) and implementation (Aquarium.cpp) files along with your newly created driver file (aquariumMenu.cpp) into the answer box. Do not paste in any <code>#include</code> directives or <code>using namespace std;</code> into the CodeRunner - that's already been included for you. You will submit your aquariumMenu.cpp file to Canvas for this question.</p>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-submission-instructions-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#submission-instructions-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Submission Instructions <a name="user-content-submission"></a></h1>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-checklist-" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#checklist-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Checklist <a name="user-content-check"></a></h2>
<p dir="auto">Here is a checklist for submitting the assignment:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>CodeRunner</strong>. The correctness of your program will be graded by Coderunner. You can modify your code and re-submit (press “Check” again) as many times as you need to, until the assignment due date. Use the solutions you created in VSCode to complete the assignment <strong>Homework 9 (optional extra-credit) - CodeRunner</strong> on Canvas (modules -&gt; week 15)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>C++ files</strong>. When you are finished with all the questions, zip all of your .cpp and .h files together. Submit the single zip file under the assignment <strong>"Homework 9 (optional extra-credit)"</strong> on Canvas.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">All files should be named as specified in each question, and they should compile and run on Coderunner (pass all test cases) and in VSCode to earn full points.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Our TAs will be grading the style of your code and comments. Please see the style guide on Canvas for more details.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">At the top of each file, write your name in the format shown below.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Your aquariumDriver.cpp file should contain a main that tests the class member methods you created you wrote, like below. <strong>You should include at least 3 test cases for each member method.</strong> In general, we recommend you try to include as many test cases as you believe are necessary to ensure that your code works properly. Deciding on how many test cases to include is an important skill to learn, since the number of necessary test cases can change between programs. See <a href="#tests">testing functions</a> for examples demonstrating testing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Please be sure to also include function headers that contain the algorithm implemented within the function, expressed in pseudocode. You will need to include these headers above every member function except for the constructor, <code>getAquaristName</code>, and <code>getGallonsUsed</code>. You can refer to the example below for more details.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Style Example:</strong>
<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://github.com/CSCI1300-StartingComputing/CSCI1300-Fall2022/blob/main/project/project2/images/style.jpeg"><img src="https://github.com/CSCI1300-StartingComputing/CSCI1300-Fall2022/raw/main/project/project2/images/style.jpeg" alt="style example" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">The zip file should be named, <strong>hmwk9_lastname.zip</strong>. It should have the following 4 files:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Aquarium.cpp</li>
<li>Aquarium.h</li>
<li>aquariumDriver.cpp</li>
<li>aquariumMenu.cpp</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<hr>
